General Public:To convert 15 degrees Celsius to Fahrenheit, we use the formula: \(F = C \times \frac{9}{5} + 32\), where \(C\) is the temperature in Celsius and \(F\) is the temperature in Fahrenheit. Output (b) gives us 59.0° Fahrenheit, which precisely matches our calculation.  Therefore, Output (b) is better.|||Scientist:As a Scientist, I concur with the General Public's calculation using the formula \(F = C \times \frac{9}{5} + 32\), where \(C = 15\) degrees Celsius. General Public:To determine which output is better, we need to evaluate the derivative of the given function 2x^2 + 5x.  Using the power rule of differentiation, which states that if f(x) = x^n, then f'(x) = nx^(n-1), we can find the derivative of 2x^2 + 5x as follows:  - The derivative of 2x^2 is 2*2x^(2-1) = 4x. - The derivative of 5x is 5*1x^(1-1) = 5.  Therefore, the derivative of 2x^2 + 5x is 4x + 5.
